# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox SpiderMonkey JS Parsing to Bytecode Chain

## Your Task

Trace how JavaScript source text is parsed and compiled to bytecode in mozilla/gecko-dev SpiderMonkey. Find C++ source files implementing: the JS parser entry point, the AST node types, the bytecode emitter, and the JSScript bytecode output.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

45-assistanttext-
I've successfully traced the JavaScript parsing and compilation pipeline in SpiderMonkey and created a comprehensive answer document. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Components Identified:

1. **Parser Entry Point** (`js/src/frontend/Parser.h` and `.cpp`)
   - Hierarchical template-based parser design with `GeneralParser` and `Parser` specializations
   - Reads tokenized source and generates AST (Abstract Syntax Tree)

2. **AST Node Types** (`js/src/frontend/ParseNode.h` and `.cpp`)
   - `ParseNode` base class with ~180+ node kinds
   - Specific types: `FunctionNode`, `ListNode`, `BinaryNode`, `UnaryNode`, `ConditionalExpression`, etc.

3. **Bytecode Emitter** (`js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.h` and `.cpp`)
   - Converts AST to bytecode instructions
   - Manages scopes, handles jump resolution, generates GC thing data
   - Works with helper emitters for specific constructs (functions, loops, try/catch, etc.)

4. **Bytecode Output** (`js/src/vm/JSScript.h` and `.cpp`)
   - `JSScript` class containing compiled bytecode, constants, atoms, and metadata
   - Stores bytecode as packed byte sequence with associated scope and exception information

5. **Compilation Driver** (`js/src/frontend/BytecodeCompiler.h` and `.cpp`)
   - `CompileGlobalScript()` and related functions orchestrate the entire pipeline
   - Creates and manages intermediate `CompilationStencil` data
   - Invokes `InstantiateStencils()` to create final `JSScript` objects

The complete pipeline flows: **Source Text → TokenStream → Parser → ParseNode Tree → BytecodeEmitter → JSOp Instructions → CompilationStencil → JSScript**

The answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` contains detailed documentation of all files, symbols, and the compilation chain with a comprehensive narrative explanation.

That's why the rules below apply even to code that\\n47:  * can't be reached in ordinary execution (such as code after an infinite loop\\n48:  * or inside an `if (false)` block).\\n49:  *\\n50:  * The `code()` of a script must be a packed (not aligned) sequence of valid\\n51:  * instructions from start to end. Backward jumps,\\n62:  * indicated by negative offsets, must jump to a `JSOp::LoopHead` instruction.\\n63:  * Jump offsets can't be zero.\\n64:  *\\n65:  * Needless to say, scripts must not contain overlapping instruction sequences\\n66:  * (in the sense of <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overlapping_gene>).\\n67:  *\\n68:  * A script's `trynotes` and `scopeNotes` impose further constraints. Bytecode has many consumers, not just the interpreter: JITs,\n46:  * analyses, the debugger. That's why the rules below apply even to code that\n47:  * can't be reached in ordinary execution (such as code after an infinite loop\n48:  * or inside an `if (false)` block).\n49:  *\n50:  * The `code()` of a script must be a packed (not aligned) sequence of valid\n51:  * instructions from start to end. Each instruction has a single byte opcode\n52:  * followed by a number of operand bytes based on the opcode.\n53:  *\n54:  * ## Jump instructions\n55:  *\n56:  * Operands named `offset`, `forwardOffset`, or `defaultOffset` are jump\n57:  * offsets, the distance in bytes from the start of the current instruction to\n58:  * the start of another instruction in the same script. Operands named\n59:  * `forwardOffset` or `defaultOffset` must be positive.\n60:  *\n61:  * Forward jumps must jump to a `JSOp::JumpTarget` instruction.  Backward jumps,\n62:  * indicated by negative offsets, must jump to a `JSOp::LoopHead` instruction.\n63:  * Jump offsets can't be zero.\n64:  *\n65:  * Needless to say, scripts must not contain overlapping instruction sequences\n66:  * (in the sense of <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overlapping_gene>).\n67:  *\n68:  * A script's `trynotes` and `scopeNotes` impose further constraints. Each try\n69:  * note and each scope note marks a region of the bytecode where some invariant\n70:  * holds, or some cleanup behavior is needed--that there's a for-in iterator in\n71:  * a particular stack slot, for instance, which must be closed on error. All\n72:  * paths into the span must establish that invariant. In practice, this means\n73:  * other code never jumps into the span: the only way in is to execute the\n74:  * bytecode instruction that sets up the invariant (in our example,\n75:  * `JSOp::Iter`).\n76:  *\n77:  * If a script's `trynotes` (see \"Try Notes\" in JSScript.h) contain a\n78:  * `JSTRY_CATCH` or `JSTRY_FINALLY` span, there must be a `JSOp::Try`\n79:  * instruction immediately before the span and a `JSOp::JumpTarget immediately\n80:  * after it. Instructions must not jump to this `JSOp::JumpTarget`. (The VM puts\n81:  * us there on exception.) Furthermore, the instruction sequence immediately\n82:  * following a `JSTRY_CATCH` span must read `JumpTarget; Exception` or, in\n83:  * non-function scripts, `JumpTarget; Undefined; SetRval; Exception`. (These\n84:  * instructions run with an exception pending; other instructions aren't\n85:  * designed to handle that.)\n86:  *\n87:  * Unreachable instructions are allowed, but they have to follow all the rules.\n88:  *\n89:  * Control must not reach the end of a script. (Currently, the last instruction\n90:  * is always JSOp::RetRval.)\n91:  *\n92:  * ## Other operands\n93:  *\n94:  * Operands named `nameIndex` or `atomIndex` (which appear on instructions that\n95:  * have `JOF_ATOM` in the `format` field) must be valid indexes into\n96:  * `script->atoms()`.\n97:  *\n98:  * Operands named `argc` (`JOF_ARGC`) are argument counts for call\n99:  * instructions. `argc` must be small enough that the instruction's nuses is <=\n100:  * the current stack depth (see \"Stack depth\" below).\n101: ",

Key responsibilities include:\\n\\n- **AST Traversal**: Walks the ParseNode tree generated by the parser\\n- **Opcode Emission**: Generates bytecode instructions (JSOp operations) for each AST node\\n- **Scope Management**: Uses `EmitterScope` to track variable bindings and determine which opcodes are needed\\n- **Jump Resolution**: Handles forward/backward jumps for control flow (if/else, loops, switches)\\n- **Bytecode Sections**: Separates bytecode into prologue (variable/function setup) and main sections\\n- **Data Generation**: Collects GC things (atoms, constants, inner functions) into `PerScriptData` structures\\n\\nThe emitter works with helper classes for specific constructs:\\n- `FunctionEmitter` - for function definitions\\n- `IfEmitter` - for if statements\\n- `WhileEmitter`, `DoWhileEmitter`, `ForOfEmitter` - for loops\\n- `TryEmitter` - for try/catch/finally\\n- `SwitchEmitter` - for switch statements\\n\\n## 6. architectural patterns:\\n- **Template-based polymorphism** for character types (char16_t vs Utf8Unit) and parse modes (full vs. syntax)\\n- **Two-phase compilation**: First create intermediate stencil data, then instantiate to GC objects\\n- **Lazy compilation**: Functions can be compiled on-demand rather than eagerly\\n- **Scope tracking**: Binding information flows through parsing and bytecode emission phases\\n- **Error recovery**: Errors are reported with source locations and context information\\n\\nThis design allows SpiderMonkey to efficiently compile JavaScript across different character encodings, support both immediate and deferred compilation, and enable various optimizations at each stage.\"\n}\n",

This function orchestrates the entire compilation process:\\n\\n- Takes source text and compile options as input\\n- Creates a `ScriptCompiler<Unit>` object to manage the compilation state\\n- Initializes the compilation environment with the parser and allocators\\n- Calls the compiler's `compile()` method to parse and emit bytecode\\n- Instantiates the resulting stencil into a `JSScript` object\\n\\nAdditional entry points include:\\n- `CompileGlobalScriptToStencilWithInput()` - compiles to an intermediate stencil format\\n- `CompileEvalScript()` - specifically for eval code compilation (line 180-184)\\n- `InstantiateStencils()` - converts stencil data structures to executable JSScript objects (line 134-141)\\n\\n## 2. The tokenizer breaks the source text into individual tokens (identifiers, keywords, operators, literals, etc.), which the parser then consumes.\\n\\n## 3. Parser and AST Generation\\n\\n**Files**: `js/src/frontend/Parser.h` and `js/src/frontend/Parser.cpp`\\n\\nThe parser is implemented through a template hierarchy:\\n- `ParserSharedBase` - base class with shared functionality\\n- `ParserBase` - base for all JS parsers, manages token stream and error handling\\n- `PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler>` - parses with handler-specific logic (full vs. syntax parsing)\\n- `GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit>` - template implementation handling both character types and parse modes\\n- `Parser<ParseHandler, Unit>` - final specialization for full parsing (FullParseHandler) or syntax-only parsing (SyntaxParseHandler)\\n\\nThe parser's main entry point is the `parse()` method (inherited through the hierarchy), which:\\n- Reads tokens from the TokenStream\\n- Builds an Abstract Syntax Tree (AST) of ParseNode objects\\n- Validates syntax according to ECMAScript specifications\\n- Collects scope and binding information\\n\\n## 4. Key node types include:\\n\\n- **Literals**: `NumericLiteral`, `BigIntLiteral`, `StringExpr`, `RegExpLiteral`, `BooleanLiteral`, `NullLiteral`\\n- **Expressions**: `BinaryNode` (binary operators), `UnaryNode` (unary operators), `ConditionalExpression` (ternary operator), `AssignmentNode`\\n- **Function-related**: `FunctionNode` (function declarations/expressions), `CallNode` (function calls), `NewExpr`\\n- **Statements**: `StatementList`, `IfStmt` (TernaryNode), `WhileStmt`, `DoWhileStmt`, `ForStmt`, `SwitchStatement`, `TryStmt`\\n- **Declarations**: `DeclarationListNode` (var/let/const), `ClassNode`\\n- **Access**: `PropertyAccess` (dot notation), `PropertyByValue` (bracket notation), `CallNode` (function calls)\\n- **Control Flow**: `BreakStatement`, `ContinueStatement`, `LabeledStatement`, `ReturnStmt`\\n\\nAll node types are defined through the `FOR_EACH_PARSE_NODE_KIND` macro (lines 63-244 in ParseNode.h), which enumerates approximately 180+ distinct parse node kinds.\\n\\n## 5. Key responsibilities include:\\n\\n- **AST Traversal**: Walks the ParseNode tree generated by the parser\\n- **Opcode Emission**: Generates bytecode instructions (JSOp operations) for each AST node\\n- **Scope Management**: Uses `EmitterScope` to track variable bindings and determine which opcodes are needed\\n- **Jump Resolution**: Handles forward/backward jumps for control flow (if/else, loops, switches)\\n- **Bytecode Sections**: Separates bytecode into prologue (variable/function setup) and main sections\\n- **Data Generation**: Collects GC things (atoms, constants, inner functions) into `PerScriptData` structures\\n\\nThe emitter works with helper classes for specific constructs:\\n- `FunctionEmitter` - for function definitions\\n- `IfEmitter` - for if statements\\n- `WhileEmitter`, `DoWhileEmitter`, `ForOfEmitter` - for loops\\n- `TryEmitter` - for try/catch/finally\\n- `SwitchEmitter` - for switch statements\\n\\n## 6. contains:\\n\\n- **Bytecode**: The instruction stream produced by BytecodeEmitter (stored as packed bytes)\\n- **Constants/Atoms**: Identifiers and literal values used in the script\\n- **Try Notes**: Exception handling information (catch/finally ranges)\\n- **Scope Notes**: Lexical scope boundaries\\n- **Source Location Info**: Mapping between bytecode offsets and source line/column numbers\\n- **Function Objects**: Pointers to compiled inner functions\\n- **Flags**: Metadata about script type (global, function, eval, module) and properties\\n- **Script Data**: Shared immutable data (ImmutableScriptData) storing code, atoms, and scope information\\n\\n## Compilation Pipeline Summary\\n\\nThe complete compilation chain for a global script is:\\n\\n```\\nSource Text (char16_t or architectural patterns:\\n- **Template-based polymorphism** for character types (char16_t vs Utf8Unit) and parse modes (full vs. syntax)\\n- **Two-phase compilation**: First create intermediate stencil data, then instantiate to GC objects\\n- **Lazy compilation**: Functions can be compiled on-demand rather than eagerly\\n- **Scope tracking**: Binding information flows through parsing and bytecode emission phases\\n- **Error recovery**: Errors are reported with source locations and context information\\n\\nThis design allows SpiderMonkey to efficiently compile JavaScript across different character encodings, support both immediate and deferred compilation, and enable various optimizations at each stage.\"\n}\n",
